  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3b8ae054-2dd5-446d-ac84-fe823988da2b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

  <span id="freeText8510507519972956214" style="display:none">He sold her the game, and Jenny Thornton walked out mesmerized by Julian, the gorgeous cyber-punk with electric blue eyes and frost-white hair. When she and her friends open the plain white box at her boyfriend Tom’s birthday party, she chills to the warning: “Entering the Shadow World can be deadly. Do so at your own risk.” Spellbound, they piece together the rooms with their darkest nightmares. Suddenly the game is real! They’re in the house of horrors, running from The Shadow Man – Julian himself, who forces them to confront their worst nightmares or be lost in a private hell. It’s Julian’s game, and Jenny is the prize he’s stalked for years. He’ll do anything to win her as she bargains desperately for her body – and soul . . .</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134287427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18427967743971252806">Julian is one of the sexiest characters in the whole of literature, seriously. Even if the story hadn't been a wonderful and gripping adventure with an array of colourful and interesting characters, it would still have been worth the read for Julian. But that aside, the book was wonderful, as soon as I finished it I instantly picked up the sequal. What a great and original story, a bit scary in parts but always entertaining - I couldn't put it down.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2061927724&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2061927724" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17381037430289501767"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/88495.The_Hunter__The_Forbidden_Game___1_' title='The Hunter (The Forbidden Game, #1) by L.J. Smith' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hunter</a> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/50873.L_J__Smith' title='L.J. Smith' rel='nofollow noopener'>L.J. Smith</a> tells the story of Jenny, who buys this game for her boyfriends birthday. This game is unique. They must face their darkest fears controlled by the shadow man, also known as Julian, a boy who is in love with Jenny.<br/><br/>They must win the game. <div id="review_2651342925" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2651342925" />
    <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink"><img alt="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568991289p2/50044222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2651342925?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink">Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2651342925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer199593170804242891">Ahhh I'm sad. The idea of this book is SO GOOD, and to be honest with you, I probably would have loved this as a teen. So, take this review with a grain of salt! The story probably works for the intended audience, which I am not. I'm also going to be a bit lenient because the book came out a long time ago and feels a bit dated (not in a bad way - but it was a different era for YA literature).<br/><br/>Listen. Anything with a villain love interest will catch my attention. But when a boy pops out of now her</span>
  <span id="freeText199593170804242891" style="display:none">Ahhh I'm sad. The idea of this book is SO GOOD, and to be honest with you, I probably would have loved this as a teen. So, take this review with a grain of salt! The story probably works for the intended audience, which I am not. I'm also going to be a bit lenient because the book came out a long time ago and feels a bit dated (not in a bad way - but it was a different era for YA literature).<br /><br />Listen. Anything with a villain love interest will catch my attention. But when a boy pops out of now here and makes love declarations to a girl for absolutely no reason, at the beginning of the book, I get a little turned off. Instant attraction and infatuation - I'm ALL game for that. But Julian basically meets Jenny and tells her right off that he's in love with her. <br /><br />*Light spoilers below*<br /><br />Now, to be fair, when things are explained later on, it made so much more sense - but I wanted so much more. Like, okay, he saw her at a young age and has been watching after her ever since - and this basically turns into a Hades/Persephone thing. And though that's creepy AF, I could still get on board for the ride. I would have at least UNDERSTOOD his reasons. But for the majority of the book, it's just a "Hey we should be together but there's NO REASON for it" deal. And I just didn't get it, because Jenny herself barely has any redeeming qualities. She's fairly bland, though at least she as some determination to get away from Julian. (Unless he kisses her, and then she's a puddle)<br /><br />Anyway, it was a really fast read, and I'm certainly not intending to trash it. LJ Smith is a respected author and I totally see why. The premise here is fantastic, and I get why people were raving about it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="199593170804242891" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11882370710276604061" style="display:none">To anyone who has ever loved Labyrinth, you would think this novel somehow tells the history of The Goblin King. They black out.<br /><br />They are in the house and the boy from the store who is a Shadow Man named Julian. <div id="review_15044217" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/15044217" />
    <a title="notyourmonkey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/122744-notyourmonkey"><img alt="notyourmonkey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1181276076p2/122744.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/15044217?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="notyourmonkey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="notyourmonkey" href="/user/show/122744-notyourmonkey">notyourmonkey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/122744-notyourmonkey?shelf=2008">2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/122744-notyourmonkey?shelf=genre-horror">genre-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/122744-notyourmonkey?shelf=genre-youngadult">genre-youngadult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/122744-notyourmonkey?shelf=belongsto-me">belongsto-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer15044217&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer15044217" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2630759105090200776">L.J. Smith is <i>such</i> a guilty pleasure of mine. I discovered her in sixth grade and have never really given her up. I didn't stumble upon this trilogy until three years ago or so, when I was living at home, marginally employed, and mildly depressed - so, hey, just about as miserable as I was in sixth grade! - and the brain-numbing cheesiness combined with just enough creativity and genuinely intriguing characters was just as soothing then as it was in middle school. <br/><br/>The first and third books of Fo</span>
  <span id="freeText2630759105090200776" style="display:none">L.J. Smith is <i>such</i> a guilty pleasure of mine. I discovered her in sixth grade and have never really given her up. I didn't stumble upon this trilogy until three years ago or so, when I was living at home, marginally employed, and mildly depressed - so, hey, just about as miserable as I was in sixth grade! - and the brain-numbing cheesiness combined with just enough creativity and genuinely intriguing characters was just as soothing then as it was in middle school. <br /><br />The first and third books of Forbidden Game are my favorites, just because of the framework they use. In book one, the titular game is a paper house that becomes real, that sucks Our Heroes into its alternate reality, and makes them face their worst nightmares. I don't care <i>how</i> cheesy the rest of it is; that's <i>cool</i>. <br /><br />Our Heroine is, as always, irritatingly perfect, though I find Jenny to come by her "perfection" a little more honestly than some of the other L.J. Smith heroines. Our Hero is even more irritating than normal, moving from starts out looking like a creepy, almost emotionally abusive and controlling relationship with Jenny to an I'm-not-worthy-must-hide-myself-from-your-perfection thing by the end of this book. (And it just gets weirder and worse as the books go on.)<br /><br />Then, of course, there is Our Villain, who is almost always more interesting, more complex, and not villainy enough to counterbalance how much nicer he is to Our Heroine than Our Hero is. Julian remains one of Smith's kickass villains. He loves Jenny, yes he does, and there's a good <i>reason</i> why it's her and no other. He is descended from a race of monsters, but there's a (okay, less good, but still plausible) <i>reason</i> why he is less monstery. He's got just enough zazz in him to make you think he might actually harm the rest of The Gang, but you never (I never) really believe he's going to harm Jenny. It's an interesting set-up. <br /><br />Plus, these books get total props for a) actually killing people and 2) even the people who end up not dead, you actually <i>think</i> are dead for a good long while. Horror movies are so much more thrilling when people might actually get knocked off. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2630759105090200776" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Lacey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21217381-lacey"><img alt="Lacey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588832316p2/21217381.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3226601495?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lacey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lacey" href="/user/show/21217381-lacey">Lacey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21217381-lacey?shelf=fantasy-paranormal">fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21217381-lacey?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21217381-lacey?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3226601495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer55136589860695424">I so badly wanted to love this book. It was so hyped up by so many self-proclaimed literature snobs who would normally turn up their noses at this sort of book that I was totally convinced I would fall in love with it and regret all the years it hadn't been in my life. <br/><br/>I guess those expectations were just too high, especially with regard to Julian, that I really only have myself to blame for being let down. I really should know better by now not to get swept up on the hype train. It's not like t</span>
  <span id="freeText55136589860695424" style="display:none">I so badly wanted to love this book. It was so hyped up by so many self-proclaimed literature snobs who would normally turn up their noses at this sort of book that I was totally convinced I would fall in love with it and regret all the years it hadn't been in my life. <br /><br />I guess those expectations were just too high, especially with regard to Julian, that I really only have myself to blame for being let down. I really should know better by now not to get swept up on the hype train. It's not like this is the first time I've been burned. Nevertheless, I kept telling myself that the book would pick up as it went on, only to have those hopes shot in the face when I got to the last page and it hadn't magically become The Best Thing Since Sliced Bread™. Big sad.<br /><br />I haven't decided yet whether I'm going to finish the series. I'm still reeling from the disappointment. I'll eventually probably pick up the next two books when I'm between books and looking for something short and fun-ish to read in the interim.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1712221972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4152682667154012343">The perfect nightmare. <i>The Forbidden Game</i> is truly one-of-a-kind for its genre. I have an ambivalence leaning towards dislike of paranormal romance, but this promised something new, and I'm glad I gave it a chance.<br/><br/>The 'romance' is more of a one-sided obsession, which Julian, an inhumanly beautiful crafter of nightmares has with the heroine, who has to outwit him to escape when he traps her and her friends in a labyrinth of their own fears.<br/>It is a fittingly nightmarish and creepy story, and I've </span>
  <span id="freeText4152682667154012343" style="display:none">The perfect nightmare. <i>The Forbidden Game</i> is truly one-of-a-kind for its genre. I have an ambivalence leaning towards dislike of paranormal romance, but this promised something new, and I'm glad I gave it a chance.<br /><br />The 'romance' is more of a one-sided obsession, which Julian, an inhumanly beautiful crafter of nightmares has with the heroine, who has to outwit him to escape when he traps her and her friends in a labyrinth of their own fears.<br />It is a fittingly nightmarish and creepy story, and I've grown to really appreciate how the relationship between the heroine and Julian is handled - it isn't insta-love, nor does she easily forgive him when his actions are monstrous. Even to the end, she would rather save her friends and herself from this horrific dreamworld.<br /><br />And speaking of, the dreamworld of this book is <i>wonderful</i> - it is haunting and strange, and vividly described to the point where you'd almost want to live there. Well, if not for the fact that it becomes what you fear the most.<br /><br />Story - 5/5<br />Characterization - 4.5/5<br />World Building - 5/5<br />General - 5/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="4152682667154012343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer695509875384518221">Jenny gets more than she bargained for when she buys a mysterious game from a strange story that she stumbled into one day. She and her friends get sucked into a strange house and are forced to face their nightmares. They must face their fears and reach the top floor in order to win. The house is controlled by Julian, a Shadow Man, who claims to be in love with Jenny. If she and her friends lose the game, Jenny must stay with him in the Shadow Realm forever.   <span id="freeText695509875384518221" style="display:none">Jenny gets more than she bargained for when she buys a mysterious game from a strange story that she stumbled into one day. She and her friends get sucked into a strange house and are forced to face their nightmares. They must face their fears and reach the top floor in order to win. The house is controlled by Julian, a Shadow Man, who claims to be in love with Jenny. If she and her friends lose the game, Jenny must stay with him in the Shadow Realm forever. Dun, dun, Duuuuunnnnn!<br /><br />I enjoyed this book. It was interesting to see what each character was afraid of as they had to face their fears. I read a lot of young teen books to preview them for our school library, and I think I might suggest it to the librarian if she doesn't already have it. There is no bad language. The characters are juniors in high school and have paired up into boyfriend/girlfriend, but really only kissing occurs between them (i.e. no sex). As far as violence goes, there isn't much. It's supposed to be a scary book, and they are living their nightmares and can potentially die from their fears, but there is no graphic violence in the book.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3450346310698872396">(Source: I own a copy of this book.)<br/>16-year-old Jenny is just looking for a party game when she comes across a strange store, and a gorgeous boy who wants to sell her exactly what she wants.<br/>What is the game that Julian sells her? And will Jenny and her friends make it to the end alive?<br/><br/><br/>I haven’t read this book for years, but thankfully it was as good as I remembered.<br/><br/>I liked Jenny although she did irritate me a bit at times. As fearless as she was in some respects, she was a bit of a pushover when</span>
  <span id="freeText3450346310698872396" style="display:none">(Source: I own a copy of this book.)<br />16-year-old Jenny is just looking for a party game when she comes across a strange store, and a gorgeous boy who wants to sell her exactly what she wants.<br />What is the game that Julian sells her? And will Jenny and her friends make it to the end alive?<br /><br /><br />I haven’t read this book for years, but thankfully it was as good as I remembered.<br /><br />I liked Jenny although she did irritate me a bit at times. As fearless as she was in some respects, she was a bit of a pushover when it came to her boyfriend and her friends, and seemed to want to do anything to please them.<br /><br />The storyline in this was pretty good, a bit of a Jumanji meets Labyrinth kind of thing, and I liked that the nightmares that each player faced were actually pretty creepy.<br />My favourite part of this book was definitely Julian though. I don’t care that he is supposed to be the bad guy; he’s just so charismatic and charming that I would have stayed with him in a heartbeat. What was Jenny thinking – she should totally choose Julian!<br />The ending was a bit of a cliff-hanger and to be honest I can’t really remember what happens in the second book, but I do remember that we get more romantic scenes with Julian! Yay!<br />Overall; a good paranormal adventure story, with a little bit of romance,<br />8.5 out of 10.<br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer12437039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14585216575118198812">Book 1 of 3. The Forbidden Game trilogy. Very good. Middle school level reading. However, has many classic themes that all ages will enjoy. Find, read, and re-read! (put on keeper shelf!)<br/><br/>The first book in the trilogy which introduces Jenny and group (her boyfriend Tom, her cousin Zach, her friends Audrey, Michael, (who are dating each other) and Dee) to the Shadow Man- Julian who has fallen in love with Jenny and won’t rest until she is his. Jenny buys The Game from Julian (unbeknownst to her at</span>
  <span id="freeText14585216575118198812" style="display:none">Book 1 of 3. The Forbidden Game trilogy. Very good. Middle school level reading. However, has many classic themes that all ages will enjoy. Find, read, and re-read! (put on keeper shelf!)<br /><br />The first book in the trilogy which introduces Jenny and group (her boyfriend Tom, her cousin Zach, her friends Audrey, Michael, (who are dating each other) and Dee) to the Shadow Man- Julian who has fallen in love with Jenny and won’t rest until she is his. Jenny buys The Game from Julian (unbeknownst to her at the time) for Tom’s birthday party. The Game is a board game of sorts that looks like a Victorian Doll House. They each draw their own faces on the characters, have to draw their own worst nightmares and swear that The Game is real and dangerous. The Game turns real and the group finds themselves actually inside The Game in the Shadow World. They each have to face their own nightmares and get to the end (the top of the house) and threw the door before dawn strikes or else Julian wins and he gets to keep Jenny forever.<br /><br />I love this story. I love the characters and the story-line even though it is young-adult and seems a little silly at times. I think it’s the nostalgia of it for me. One of my all time favorite books/trilogies. In this trilogy though, I always root for the bad guy. I can’t help it, I LOVE Julian. :o) <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14585216575118198812" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2563040528" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2563040528" />
    <a title="Vanessa (bookfairy95)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64363186-vanessa-bookfairy95"><img alt="Vanessa (bookfairy95)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586342217p2/64363186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2563040528?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vanessa (bookfairy95)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vanessa (bookfairy95)" href="/user/show/64363186-vanessa-bookfairy95">Vanessa (bookfairy95)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64363186-vanessa-bookfairy95?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2563040528&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2563040528" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17460081332372646574">Okay, this is going to be a short review.<br/><br/>I liked this a lot! It's a bit old school, but that's to be expected, since it is from 1994.<br/>I also got huge Jumanji vibes from this, with the whole being-sucked-into-a-game scenario. <br/><br/>The characters were all great and different and well developed and even though each and every one of them had a clear role and a specific character, they didn't feel like stereotypes to me. <br/>Julian was just amazing. He is so interesting and dark and handsome and he is the vill</span>
  <span id="freeText17460081332372646574" style="display:none">Okay, this is going to be a short review.<br /><br />I liked this a lot! It's a bit old school, but that's to be expected, since it is from 1994.<br />I also got huge Jumanji vibes from this, with the whole being-sucked-into-a-game scenario. <br /><br />The characters were all great and different and well developed and even though each and every one of them had a clear role and a specific character, they didn't feel like stereotypes to me. <br />Julian was just amazing. He is so interesting and dark and handsome and he is the villain. Yeah... I got that, but I couldn't help but love him. His character is twisted and even though he does everything to get what he is after, he also has this "soft" side to him. He is not really soft, but he has something about him that is charming and almost... tender? I don't really know how I should describe him. But I wanted Jenny to stay with him, even though I somehow knew she wouldn't. Such a shame though!!! <br />Tom on the other hand was kind of lame. (Sorry to everyone who liked him.) He didn't play a very big role in this book (as he was away almost the entire time), but Jenny kept thinking about him to remind herself that she shouldn't want and think about Julian. That was also kind of meh. I like that she wanted to stay loyal, but at the same time she kept kissing Julian (and enjoying it) and kept thinking about him oh so often, so it didn't really make sense. But oh well...<br /><br />A unique aspect in this book were the nightmare of the different characters. While being kidnapped by aliens was still a somewhat "normal" fear, the other nightmares were something completely original. The author seemed to have thought a lot about these nightmares and I think they were excellent! <br /><br />Finally, the book is really short and you can fly through it and finish it within a few days even if you don't have time and only read on the train to work - like me. So, if you wanna read something fast and somewhat original over Halloween (somewhat, because the game aspect reminded me of Jumanji), go for it!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_348541822" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/348541822" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/348541822?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer348541822" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14710319648602432182">I think it would be an understatement to say that I am impressed by L.J. Smith. Smith's name is one that is familiar to nearly everyone, if not for anything else then for her widely popular <i> Vampire Diaries </i> Series. I was more than a little nervous going into <i> The Forbidden Game </i> though, merely because I wanted to like her just as much as everyone else did. I wanted to fall in love with her characters and her world and I can assure you, there are very few authors who I <i> really </i> want to love. I a</span>
  <span id="freeText14710319648602432182" style="display:none">I think it would be an understatement to say that I am impressed by L.J. Smith. Smith's name is one that is familiar to nearly everyone, if not for anything else then for her widely popular <i> Vampire Diaries </i> Series. I was more than a little nervous going into <i> The Forbidden Game </i> though, merely because I wanted to like her just as much as everyone else did. I wanted to fall in love with her characters and her world and I can assure you, there are very few authors who I <i> really </i> want to love. I am glad to say however, that L.J. Smith did not disappoint. If anything, she made it easy for me to join the ranks of her avid fans. <br /><br /><i> The Hunter </i> is possibly one of the scariest novels I've read. It begins when Jenny, searching for an interesting game to play at her boyfriend's birthday party, stumbles upon a mysterious store and an even more mysterious owner. Julian, the enigmatic and beautiful man she meets, offers her The Game and she takes it home with a strange feeling in her heart. It turns out that The Game is merely a dollhouse - one which her boyfriend Tom, best friends Dee, Audrey, and Summer, cousin Zach, and other close friend Michael, all eagerly complete. Yet, what they don't expect is to find themselves <i> inside </i> the dollhouse, facing their worst nightmares, for Julian isn't what he seems to be. He is The Shadow Man and he wants Jenny. If Jenny and her friends can't make it out of the dollhouse alive before dawn, they'll be trapped in there - forever. <br /><br />I knew, even before starting this book, that it was going to be a page-turning thriller, but I somehow never anticipated it to be as good as it was. L.J. Smith's work was published long before any of the current YA fluff we read, so it's obvious that her ideas were the original multi-dimensional world, creepy stalker, and practically insta-love tales. Needless to say, they are full of the depth, mystery, and horror that current YA fiction is lacking. I absolutely loved the rich realm that Smith created. Her writing is gripping, her descriptions mesmerizing, and if you yourself don't feel as if you're in this haunted doll house, then you're reading the wrong book.<br /><br />I also fell in love with every single one of Smith's characters, except Julian of course. Julian is <i> creepy. </i> He is the kind of guy you hope never to meet in your life (if you ever do meet him, run the opposite direction as fast as you possibly can). Although he is insane, psychotic, and more than a little sadistic, I found him to be incredibly entertaining and his dialogue gave me the chills. I thought the way in which the other characters dealt with him was very realistic and I absolutely adore Jenny as a protagonist. She is kind, brave, courageous, strong, and doesn't give in to Julian's temptations. Of her friends, Dee was by far my favorite as she could truly be a warrior-princess. Audrey is intelligent, Zach is mysterious but calm and cool, Michael is simply adorable and sweet, Summer is naive, and Tom is...well, I didn't develop too much of feeling towards Tom in this book. Honestly, we didn't really get to know him. He appeared in the very beginning and again towards the end, but I'm going to go ahead and tell you that I fell in love with him in the sequel!(: <br /><br />I think what I love best about Smith's novel is the fact that she is able to find the silver lining behind the dark cloud she created. The Game is dangerous and terrifying and not everyone gets out alive; yet, Smith shows us how this ordeal has changed her characters - for the better. They have learned more, trusted further, and come to appreciate all that they have. That, more than anything else, is what struck out to me as being important in this book. <i> The Hunter </i> was definitely an entertaining read, but at the end of the day, it proved to be one with a deeper message as well. I have to warn you though, this story ends with a cliffhanger, so if you're going to read this series, make sure you have both sequels in your grasp. <br /><br />That being said, what are you waiting for? Immerse yourself in the world of L.J. Smith and revel in its dark beauty and mystery for yourself. And remember: never trust beautiful strangers, unknown games, or make a bargain with the devil. You just may not escape alive. ;) <br /><br /><i> A HUGE thank you to Inge, my beautiful Belgian friend, for recommending this series to me. I am thoroughly enjoying it! </i> </span>
  <a data-text-id="14710319648602432182" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rae Lake" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rae Lake" href="/user/show/33679923-rae-lake">Rae Lake</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33679923-rae-lake?shelf=mmc-18">mmc-18</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2478839444&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2478839444" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15157137423655935502">This was a great book! <br/>I got a real adult goosebumps vibe from this, and then some Jumanji.<br/>So you have Jenny who is trying to throw a great party for her long term boyfriend Tom. She usually throws pool parties but this time she thinks it may be fun to throw a game party, something like charades or spin the bottle. Something along those lines. She goes into a game shop that just magically appears out of thin air... That should have been the first clue that maybe you shouldn't buy but you know...</span>
  <span id="freeText15157137423655935502" style="display:none">This was a great book! <br />I got a real adult goosebumps vibe from this, and then some Jumanji.<br />So you have Jenny who is trying to throw a great party for her long term boyfriend Tom. She usually throws pool parties but this time she thinks it may be fun to throw a game party, something like charades or spin the bottle. Something along those lines. She goes into a game shop that just magically appears out of thin air... That should have been the first clue that maybe you shouldn't buy but you know...She goes in and buys a game with no name for 20 bucks.... <br />The game turns out to be some sort of magic that brings all your worst nightmares to life. Now Jenny and her friends have to find there way to the top of the house going through each and everyone of their night mares one by one. The nightmares range from super creepy to scary. I think Summer and Michaels nightmares were the scariest. <br />Of course at the end, Jenny was able to get away buy reciting a magic word that she seemed to know from when she was a small child from her grandfather who turned out to be a sorcerer. I think this book could have been way more scary but It was good for what it was.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15157137423655935502" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1641333564" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1641333564" />
    <a title="Manna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19723258-manna"><img alt="Manna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426922465p2/19723258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1641333564?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manna" href="/user/show/19723258-manna">Manna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19723258-manna?shelf=messed-up-hotties">messed-up-hotties</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19723258-manna?shelf=icy-boys">icy-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19723258-manna?shelf=dark-and-cunning-boys">dark-and-cunning-boys</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1641333564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer62473473387900816">Took me ages to get my hand on this one. For some reason I stuck at the first few chapters for a while. But once the game began, whoosh.... <br/><br/>I love the building of suspense. It was like watching a thriller movie. All the sequence building up before the game starts. The footsteps, the reading, those 'off' feelings radiated from the Game sent me on edge. It was nice seeing Jenny, a delicate, kind-heart girl fighting with her friends. Facing fears, and at the same time trying to resist Julian...<br/><br/>Juli</span>
  <span id="freeText62473473387900816" style="display:none">Took me ages to get my hand on this one. For some reason I stuck at the first few chapters for a while. But once the game began, whoosh.... <br /><br />I love the building of suspense. It was like watching a thriller movie. All the sequence building up before the game starts. The footsteps, the reading, those 'off' feelings radiated from the Game sent me on edge. It was nice seeing Jenny, a delicate, kind-heart girl fighting with her friends. Facing fears, and at the same time trying to resist Julian...<br /><br />Julian... The Heart Throbbing Julian.<br />Julian was Pure evil. but heart throbbing. Seriously, I love the character that seems so dark, but so sensitive when it comes to love. It just drives me insane. The way he handled her with delicacy, like she could break anytime. But there were those moments when he promised that she, too, will be experiencing the game like the others.<br /><br />I just really can't guess what Julian would or would not do.<br /><br />And there's Tom...<br /><br />Okay. These two just reminds me of the Darkling and Mal.<br />And I still don't know who will be The Guy. <br />The end was a little swift, a relief for the characters, but left me curious.<br />I want to see what Jenny could do. Seems like this book is just the beginning of the Game.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[What would Julian do when he got out of the closet? Will he still crazy about her? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="62473473387900816" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_991902418" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/991902418" />
    <a title="Alexandra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/351830-alexandra"><img alt="Alexandra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568913395p2/351830.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/991902418?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexandra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexandra" href="/user/show/351830-alexandra">Alexandra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781441875396" href="/book/show/7969888-the-hunter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/351830-alexandra?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/351830-alexandra?shelf=own-on-audible">own-on-audible</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer991902418" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3608043224903479981">The premise for this story is really interesting. The execution of it however I found very bland. This left me very underwhelmed.<br/><br/>The villain isn't sexy or attractive, in my opinion. Just another, sadly typical, jerk who confuses desire to possess and control with "love".<br/><br/>The other characters seemed fairly flat and one dimensional to me. The story should have been suspenseful and even perhaps scary, but really wasn't. The situation certainly is one that should be suspenseful and scary, but the wri</span>
  <span id="freeText3608043224903479981" style="display:none">The premise for this story is really interesting. The execution of it however I found very bland. This left me very underwhelmed.<br /><br />The villain isn't sexy or attractive, in my opinion. Just another, sadly typical, jerk who confuses desire to possess and control with "love".<br /><br />The other characters seemed fairly flat and one dimensional to me. The story should have been suspenseful and even perhaps scary, but really wasn't. The situation certainly is one that should be suspenseful and scary, but the writing didn't measure up and create any real suspense or emotion.<br /><br />And the reaction to the death of one of their friends, as other reviewers has mentioned, was also strangely devoid of much emotion, and wasn't much more than a blip on their radar.<br /><br />I've seen some refer to this as middle-grade, but I would not consider it middle-grade. It seems intended as YA to me. But perhaps those thinking of this as middle-grade fiction do so because most above that age wouldn't find it very suspenseful or scary. <br /><br />Overall I was able to stick with it because it was tolerable, but am very disappointed it wasn't better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3608043224903479981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4NcjLG9JAfz3SrNiQ8AXmJvJTyVV20XjOAihOJWLbFPXQ8gEoFONWAghB5Q3hKbW1+/xcygWQa6Cq0TfmUW68A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10333281057748071209">I have a new blog about my Vampire Diaries fanfic.<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/5539821-l-j-smith-s-new-vampires-diaries-series'>https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog...</a><br/><br/><b>L.J. SMITH</b>, Lisa Jane Smith, is the New York Times #1 Bestselling author of <i>The Vampire Diaries, The Secret Circle, The Forbidden Game, Dark Visions, Wildworld</i> and <i>Night World</i> series. She has written over two dozen books for children and young adults, and has enjoyed writing every one of them. She lives in th</span>
  <span id="freeText10333281057748071209" style="display:none">I have a new blog about my Vampire Diaries fanfic.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/5539821-l-j-smith-s-new-vampires-diaries-series">https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog...</a><br /><br /><b>L.J. SMITH</b>, Lisa Jane Smith, is the New York Times #1 Bestselling author of <i>The Vampire Diaries, The Secret Circle, The Forbidden Game, Dark Visions, Wildworld</i> and <i>Night World</i> series. She has written over two dozen books for children and young adults, and has enjoyed writing every one of them. She lives in the Bay Area of California, with a backyard that is full of flowers, which she adores, especially with many different shades of roses.<br /><br />She loves to visit a friend's little cabin in the Point Reyes National Seashore area, which has lots of trees, lots of animals, lots of beaches to walk on, and lots of places to hike. Once, while hiking, she saw a snow-white buck which allowed her to follow it nearly half a mile. She also likes to collect things: angels (they remind her of her late mother), tiny boxes from different countries or of fanciful shape, nineteenth century children's literature, and books about quantum physics--especially about the mystery of the dark energy in the universe. A militant optimist, she is also part of the Velociraptor Sisterhood (a fancy way of saying that she likes to read, write and discuss books with strong female characters), and she has traveled extensively in Europe and the Far East. The two countries she loves to visit most are Great Britain, with its historic monuments and amazing country landscapes, and Japan, with its bustling urban life and exquisite mountain scenery.<br /><br />Her favorite current writer is Terry Pratchett, the author of the Discworld series, for its wild and witty satires on life, death, war, love, assassins, coppers, and Australia. Her favorite classical writer is Jane Austen. Her favorite poets are Robert Frost and Emily Dickinson. Her favorite movies are The Seven Samurai and Avatar (analyze that!). She doesn't have a favorite TV show, because she doesn't have time to watch TV (and only owns one for playing movies).<br /><br />Her favorite people are her readers, each of whom she cherishes with deep and lasting affection.<br /><br /><i>Note: L. J. Smith wrote books 1-7 of The Vampire Diaries series. After that, a ghostwriter took over the rest of the series. L. J. wrote books 1-3 of The Secret Circle series. After that, a ghostwriter took over the rest of the series. L. J. did not write any of the Originals or Stefan's Diaries. These were written by Kevin Williamson and/or various ghostwritters.</i> <br /></span>
